**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is April, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4

    First Check After Step 5

    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

**Revision Explanation:**
I reorganized the categories to better support human cognition and ensure similar topics remain grouped together. Key changes include:
1. Renamed "Trump Administration" to the broader "Executive Branch & Government Operations" to encompass all federal governance activities
2. Combined economic and budget topics under one area for clearer financial policy grouping
3. Moved environmental topics to be closer to related health and social policy themes
4. Separated education and science from economic policy for better thematic alignment
5. Refined topic descriptions to ensure each news article can find a clear best-fitting category
6. Ensured a logical flow between related areas (e.g., placing executive actions near budget decisions which implement those actions)

### 7.1 Defense & Intelligence Operations

## 2. Economy & Fiscal Policy

### 2.1 Economic Indicators & Recession Concerns
The U.S. economy demonstrated resilience in April 2025, adding 177,000 jobs, stronger than economists had anticipated [94]. However, President Trump has openly acknowledged the possibility of a recession, characterizing the current economic situation as a "transition period" and suggesting that a short-term economic downturn would be acceptable for long-term prosperity [19]. When questioned about recession risks, Trump stated that "anything can happen" [33]. The administration's promised "golden age" for the economy is facing challenges in its early implementation [68], with factual disputes emerging regarding economic claims, including GasBuddy publicly challenging statements made by Trump about fuel prices [98].

### 2.2 Budget & Trade Policies
The Trump administration has unveiled a budget proposal allocating $1 trillion for defense while implementing substantial cuts to education, foreign aid, environmental programs, health initiatives, and public assistance [38]. Specific cuts include a 40% reduction in rental aid, with the administration suggesting states could fill the funding gap if they choose [4]. The budget has received mixed reactions, with Republican defense hawks expressing dissatisfaction with aspects of the proposal [28].

The administration's tariff policies are creating significant economic ripple effects. A major health care company has reported that new tariffs will cost it between $60-70 million this year, raising concerns about higher prices and potential shortages in the health care sector [45]. Meanwhile, e-commerce platform Temu has halted direct shipping from China following the closure of the "de minimis" tariff loophole [63].

## 3. Immigration & Border Security

### 3.1 Deportation Initiatives & Enforcement
The Trump administration has developed comprehensive deportation initiatives, including plans to track approximately 450,000 migrant children through door knocks and DNA tests [18]. International negotiations are underway, with reports indicating talks with Rwanda to accept deportees from the United States [37]. The deportation campaign has led to American citizens crossing state lines seeking safety, described by some as "refugees" [87], while raising questions about the status of U.S. citizen children whose parents face deportation [90].

The administration has implemented a strict "catch and revoke" policy for visa holders, establishing a zero-tolerance approach to visa compliance [53]. Meanwhile, the Department of Justice has filed a lawsuit against Colorado and Denver over their so-called "sanctuary laws" [42], escalating tensions between federal immigration enforcement priorities and state/local policies.

## 4. Education, Science & Research

### 4.1 Scientific Research & Education Funding
The National Science Foundation has halted all funding to scientists indefinitely under the Trump administration [1], representing an unprecedented interruption in federal support for scientific research. Former Weather Service leaders have warned that staffing cuts within their agency could potentially lead to "loss of life" due to compromised forecasting and emergency response capabilities [22].

In education, Texas Governor Greg Abbott is poised to sign what is being described as the largest school voucher law in the United States [97], while the Trump administration is cutting school mental health grants that had previously enjoyed bipartisan support following the Uvalde school shooting [9]. At the state level, the Oklahoma State Department of Education has approved controversial new social studies standards [8].

## 5. Health & Social Policy

### 5.1 Healthcare Policies & Public Health
Health and Human Services (HHS) policies have taken notable turns, with RFK Jr. directing efforts to search for new measles treatments instead of emphasizing vaccination [44], despite measles being a preventable disease with existing vaccines. A top U.S. scientist has suggested that the world may be entering a "post-herd immunity" era regarding measles [92], indicating growing concerns about vaccination rates.

A new HHS report has urged "exploratory therapy" for transgender youth [59], signaling shifts in the administration's approach to gender-affirming care for minors. Meanwhile, legislation has been introduced in Congress (H.R.3154) to eliminate general Medicaid funding limitations for U.S. territories [43].

## 6. Legal & Judicial Developments

### 6.1 Court Rulings & Constitutional Challenges
A federal judge has struck down President Trump's executive order targeting the law firm Perkins Coie, ruling it unconstitutional [5]. The judge permanently blocked the order, describing it as an unprecedented action targeting a firm for representing clients and causes disliked by the president.

Supreme Court Justice Ketanji Brown Jackson has publicly criticized President Trump's attacks on the judiciary [11], marking a rare instance of a sitting justice directly confronting presidential rhetoric about the courts. Meanwhile, the Trump administration has asked the Supreme Court to grant DOGE access to Social Security data [67], raising privacy and separation of powers questions.

The Department of Justice has sent threatening letters to medical journals [55], while the Trump administration has enacted what critics describe as the "biggest rollback" of civil rights since Reconstruction [41].

The U.S. military is planning a parade to celebrate the Army's 250th anniversary, scheduled to coincide with President Trump's birthday [60]. In separate operational developments, the Trump administration is reportedly laying groundwork for potential unilateral U.S. military action against cartels in Mexico [69].

The intelligence community is experiencing significant restructuring.
